[and the third also] extr.; (L;) or the last is an inf. n. and the last but one signifies “ a praiseworthy quality, ” or “ a quality for which one is praised; ” (ElFenáree, MF;) or the last may be a simple subst.; (Har p. 392;) <hi rend="ital">He praised, eulogized,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commended, him; spoke well of him; mentioned him with approbation;</hi> (Akh, S, L, Msb;) <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">for such a thing;</hi> (L, Msb;) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذَمَّهُ</foreign>: (S, L:) accord. to IAmb, formed by transposition from <foreign lang="ar">مَدَحَ</foreign>: (marginal note in a copy of the MS:) but it is of less common application than the latter verb; (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">مدح</foreign>;) signifying <hi rend="ital">he praised him,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">for something depending on his</hi> (the latter's) <hi rend="ital">own will:</hi> thus, the describing a pearl as clear is not <foreign lang="ar">حَمْدٌ</foreign>, but it is <foreign lang="ar">مَدْحٌ</foreign>: (Kull p. 150:) or <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَهُ</foreign>: (Lh, K:) but it differs [sometimes] from this; (Msb;) for <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرٌ</foreign> is only on account of favour received; whereas <foreign lang="ar">حَمْدٌ</foreign> is sometimes because of favour received, (Th, Az, Msb,) and sometimes from other causes; (Th;) [and thus] the latter is of more common application than the former; (S;) therefore you do not say, <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى شَجَاعَتِهِ</foreign>; but you say, <foreign lang="ar">حَمِدْتُهُ على شجاعته</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I praised him,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">for his courage.</hi> (Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">حمد</foreign> also implies admiration: and it implies the magnifying, or honouring, of the object thereof; and lowliness, humility, or submissiveness, in the person who offers it; as in the saying of the afflicted, <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ لِلّٰهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Praise be to God;</hi> since in this case there is no worldly blessing, favour, or <pb n="639"/> benefit. (Msb.) This last phrase is generally pronounced as it is written above: but some of the Arabs are related to have pronounced it <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدَ لِلّٰهِ</foreign>, putting the former word in the accus. case as the absolute complement of the verb <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَدُ</foreign> understood: and others, <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدِلِلّٰهِ</foreign>; assimilating the final vowel of the former word to the vowel immediately following it: and others, <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ لُلّٰهِ</foreign>; assimilating the first vowel in <foreign lang="ar">للّٰه</foreign> to the vowel immediately preceding it: Zj, however, disapproves of the latter two modes of pronouncing it: some of them also said, <foreign lang="ar">بَدَأْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِالحَمْدُ لِلّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I began with</hi> the saying <hi rend="ital">Praise be to God.</hi> (L.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">حَمْدٌ</foreign> below.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَدُ إِلَيْكَ ٱللّٰهَ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">He affected,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made a show of,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">تَكَلَّفَ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">praise.</hi> (A.) You say,   
      <foreign lang="ar">وَجَدْتُهُ <ref cref="n9035-1" target="مُتَحَمِّدًا" n="1" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> مُتَشَكِّرًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I found him affecting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">making a show of, praise and thanks</hi>]. (A.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">He praised himself.</hi> (KL.) [Golius assigns this meaning to   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9035-2" target="احتمد" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n9037"/></foreign>, as on the authority of the KL; but it is not assigned to this verb in my copy of the KL.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَتَحَمَّدُ النّاس</foreign> [app. a slight mistranscription, for <foreign lang="ar">لِلنَّاسِ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى النَّاسِ</foreign>, as in an ex. in the next sentence but one,] <hi rend="ital">Such a one pretends to men,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">shows them, that he is praiseworthy,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِجُودِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">for his liberality.</hi> (L.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تحمّد</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He reproached him for a favour,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">benefit, which he</hi> (the former) <hi rend="ital">had bestowed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conferred;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recounted his gifts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">actions, to him;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِمْتَنَّ</foreign>. (S, L, K.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ أَنْفَقَ مَالَهُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَتَحَمَّدْ بِهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Whoso expends his property upon himself, he shall not reproach men therewith as for favours,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">benefits, bestowed</hi>]: (S, A:) or <foreign lang="ar">فلا يتحمّد بِه إِلَى النَّاسِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he shall not pretend to men that he is praiseworthy on account of it</hi>]: a prov., meaning that a man is not praised for his beneficence to himself, but for his beneficence to others.
